text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; font-family: MoinaNormal;">HC ®Q±q¢Ÿl j­dÉ 1-13(HL Nä¡ ®al ¢am) S¢j j¡œz<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">12.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He also referring the schedule of the application pointed that the land which has been transferred through the deed No. 5170 dated 24.12.2012 belong to more then one parties however, the pre-emptor in the schedule has mentioned that except share of purchaser No. 5 Ziaul Haque rest land 1 Nä¡ 13 ¢am is under the pre-emption. However, in the schedule of the application the pre-emptor did not specified the land of pre-emptee No. 5 and rest of the land which sought pre-emption by the pre-emptor. Therefore, in such unspecified and undivided land partial pre-emption cannot be allowed. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">13.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The opposite party No. 1 entered to the revisional application by filing power through one Abdul Momen Chowdhury on 02.01.2017 however, he never appeared before us although this item has been appearing in the cause list with the name of the learned Advocate for the opposite party No. 1 for few weeks. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">14.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The pre-emptee called in question the legality and propriety of the impugned order dated 11.02.2016. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">15.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Therefore, we are of the view that we must address the first question raised by the learned Advocate for the pre-emptee-petitioner. In view of the legal question as raised by the learned Advocate we must look into the provision of sub-sections 1, 2 and 3 of section 96 of the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act which runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“96. Right of Pre-emption</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"> – (1) If a portion or share of a holding of a raiyat is sold to a person who is not a co-sharer tenant in the holding, one or more co-sharer tenants of the holding may, within two months of the service of the notice given under section 98, or, if no notice has been served under section 98, within two months of the date of the knowledge of the sale, apply to the Court for the said portion or share to be sold to himself or themselves:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Provided that no application under this section shall lie unless the applicant is – </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l5 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 76.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 76.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">a co-sharer tenant in the holding by inheritance; and </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l5 level1 lfo3; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 76.5pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 76.5pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">a person to whom sale of the holding or the portion or share thereof, as the case may be, can be made under section 90:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>Provided further that no application under this section shall lie after expiry of three years from the date of registration of the sale deed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In an application under sub-section (1), all other co-sharer tenants by inheritance of the holding and the purchaser shall be made parties.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l4 level1 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">An application under sub-section (1) shall be dismissed unless the applicant or applicants, at the time of making it, deposit in the Court – </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 9.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the amount of the consideration money of the sold holding or portion or share of the holding as stated in the notice under section 89 or in the deed of sale, as the case may be; </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 9.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">               </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">compensation at the rate of twenty five per centum of the amount referred to in clause (a); and </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 9.0pt; mso-list: l0 level1 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">                </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">an amount calculated at the rate of eight per centum simple annual interest upon the amount referred to in clause (a) for the period from the date of the execution of the deed of sale to the date of filing of the application for pre-emption.<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">”</strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">16.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the above provisions of law it is apparent that the pre-emptor must deposit the amount as prescribed in clause (a), (b), and (c) of sub-section 3 of section 96 of the Act at the time of filing the pre-emption application. However, on perusal of the application for pre-emption and impugned order it is patently visible that the pre-emptor and the learned Judge of the Court below clearly admitted amount deposited less than the require amount. So, the submission advanced by the learned Advocate regarding the less deposit is sustainable which by now not a disputed question. However, the learned Judge of the trial Court has further opined that the pre-emptor filed a petition to deposit the due amount as calculated by the pre-emptee. The Court has passed an order to deposit the said less amount. The learned Judge of the Court below further opined that there is no bar to deposit the rest amount during the pendency of the case. So we have to now answer whether the opinion of the learned Joint District Judge is correct and acceptable. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">17.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. P.K. Das, the learned Advocate for the petitioner has categorically pointed that the period of time for filing of the pre-emption as stipulated in the provision of sub-section 1 of section 96 of the Act is 2 (two) months from the date of registration or from the date of knowledge. The pre-emptor has filed the application under section 96 on 29.01.2013 however, the question of depositing the rest amount has arisen while the pre-emptee filed application on 24.04.2015 and the learned Judge by his order dated 11.02.2016 allowed the pre-emptor to deposit the rest amount from the date of calculation and order.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">18.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The requirement of the law is that the deposit must be given at the time of filing of the application under section 96 of the Act. According to provision of the sub-section 4 of section 96 of the Act the deposit of requires money is a condition precedent. So, we are of the view that the sub-section 4 of section 96 of the Act be reproduced for ready reference which runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“</span></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On receipt of such application accompanied by such deposits, the Court shall give notice to the purchaser and to the other persons made parties thereto under sub-section (2) to appear within such period as it may fix and shall require the purchaser to state what other sums he has paid in respect of rent since the date of sale and what expenses he has incurred in annulling encumbrances on, or for making any improvement in respect of the holding, portion or share sold.</span></em><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">”</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">19.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the provision of sub-section 4 of section 96 of the Act it’s become crystal clear that the Court cannot register the application as pre-emption case without taking deposit of the requires amount as described in clause (a) (b) (c) of sub-section 3 of the section 96. So, in view of such condition precedent as provided in the provision of law the learned Joint District Judge directed the pre-emptor to deposit the rest due amount on 11.02.2016 which should not but must opined that such direction is not within the purview of the provisions of sub-sections 3 and 4 of section 96 of the Act. So, we are of the considered view that the opinion of the learned Joint District Judge regarding the deposit of the rest amount by the pre-emptor is not only illegal but also flagrant violation of the provisions of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>sub-sections 3 and 4 of section 96 of the Act.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">20.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We find support of our view to the case of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Mojibar Rahman Mondal (Md) Vs. Khoteza Khatoon and others </em>reported in 2 BLC 1997 (AD) 170. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">21.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It has been held in Mojibar Rahman case that the application for deposit the rest of amount was allowed by the Court below and on revision the High Court Division also upheld that order however, the Appellate Division found that legal proposition of section 96 of the Act does not allow to deposit the rest of the amount beyond the period of limitation. Therefore, we cannot but to opine that the direction for deposition of the rest of amount beyond the statutory period is clear violation of the provision of law of sub-section 3 of section 96 of the Act.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">22.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the impugned order the learned Joint District Judge further opined that there is no impediment to allow the partial pre-emption. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">23.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He has also opined that there is no such law which impede the pre-emptor to pray for the partial pre-emption. We have to give answer whether the opinion of the learned Joint District Judge is sustainable in accordance with law or not. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">24.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It has been held in the case of Arifan Nessa VS Haroon-or –Rashed and others reported 2 B.L.C (HCD) 76 that </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">State Acquisition and Tenancy Act of 1951, Section 96-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 1.8pt; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .4in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Partial pre-emption cannot be allowed-Although all the pre-emptees were brought on record except one who was impleaded in the pre-emption case after the statutory period of limitation, a valuable right has already accrued in favour of the pre-emptees for which the case must fail as partial pre-emption is not allowed under section 96 of the Act.”</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">25.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">It has been held to the case of Hatem Ali Mollah<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>@ others –VS- Hayet Khan and others reported 1986 B.C.R (AD) 237:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">State Acquisition and Tenancy Act, 1950, Section 96</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .3in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">“ <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Partial pre-emption is not permissible</em>.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: .3in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt .5in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Deposite of entire consideration money stated in the kabala was made but pre emption of only. 54</span></em><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;"><span style="mso-spacerun: yes;"> </span>acres of land out of 1.14 acres was sought- When the prayer for pre-emption was for a part of the entire land sold, the prayer cannot be read in respect of the whole when the entire consideration money stated in the kabala was deposited by the appellants. The Court is not required to make deduction otherwise in respect of the prayer.<span style="position: relative; top: 5.0pt; mso-text-raise: -5.0pt;"><img height="23" src="file:///C:\Users\User\AppData\Local\Temp\msohtmlclip1\01\clip_image002.gif" width="12"/></span></span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">26.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Therefore, in view of the above authorities we are of the opinion that learned Joint District Judge in an imperceptible manner totally misconceived regarding the settle principle enunciated by the apex Court in respect of partial pre-emption which cannot be sustained in law. So, we are unable to accept the opinion expressed by the learned Joint District Judge as well it is deprecated. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">27.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The pre-emptees filed an application under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure to reject the plaint. Now, legal question is whether the application of pre-emption case is plaint or not ? So, we are of the view that the provisions of Rules 1 to 9 and 11 Order 7 of the Code be reproduced herein below which runs as follows:-<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">1.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The plaint shall contain the following particulars:-</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the name of the Court in which the suit is brought;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the name, description and place of residence of the plaintiff;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the name, description and place of residence of the defendant, so far as they can be ascertained;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">where the plaintiff or the defendant is a minor or a person of unsound mind, a statement to that effect;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(e)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the facts constituting the cause of action and when it arose;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(f)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the facts showing that the Court has jurisdiction;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(g)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">the relief which the plaintiff claims;</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(h)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">where the plaintiff has allowed a set-off or relinquished a portion of his claim, the amount so allowed or relinquished; and</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l3 level1 lfo5; tab-stops: 63.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 63.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(i)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">     </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">a statement of the value of the subject-matter of the suit for the purposes of jurisdiction and of court-fees, so far as the case admits.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the plaintiff seeks the recovery of money, the plaint shall state the precise amount claimed:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .6in;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">But where the plaintiff sues for mesne profits, or for an amount which will be found due to him on taking unsettled accounts between him and the defendant, the plaint shall state approximately the amount sued for.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the subject-matter of the suit is immovable property, the plaint shall contain a description of the property sufficient to identify it, and , in case such property can be<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>identified by boundaries or numbers in a record of settlement of survey, the plaint shall specify such boundaries or numbers. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">4.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the plaintiff sues in a representative character the plaint shall show not only that he has an actual existing interest in the subject-matter, but that he has taken the steps (if any) necessary to enable him to institute a suit concerning it.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">5.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">The plaint shall show that the defendant is or claims to be interested in the subject-matter, and that he is liable to be called upon to answer the plaintiff’s<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>demand.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">6.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Where the suit is instituted after the expiration of the period prescribed by the law of limitation, the plaint shall show the ground upon which exemption from such law is claimed.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">7.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Every plaint shall state specifically the relief which the plaintiff claims either simply or in the alternative, and it shall not be necessary to ask for general or other relief which my always be given as the Court may think just to the same extent as it it had been asked for. A the same rule shall apply to any relief claimed by the defendant in his written statement. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">8.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the plaintiff seeks relief in respect of several distinct grounds, they shall be stated as far as may be separately and distinctly. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level2 lfo4; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 42.3pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 42.3pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">9.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">      </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(1) The plaintiff shall endorse on the plaint, or annex thereto, a list of the documents (if any) which he has produced along with it; and, if the plaint is admitted, shall present as many copies on plain paper of the plaint as there are defendants, unless the Court by reason of the length or the plaint or the number of the defendants, or for any other sufficient reason permits him to present a like number of concise statements<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>of the nature of the claim made, or of the relief claimed in the suit, in which case he shall present such statements.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 45.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(2)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the plaintiff sues, or the defendant or any of the defendants is sued, in a representative capacity, such statements shall show in what capacity the plaintiff or defendant sues or is sued. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 45.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(3)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The plaintiff may, by leave of the Court, amend such statements so as to make them correspond with the plaint.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l0 level4 lfo4; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 45.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(4)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">         </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The chief ministerial officer of the Court shall sign such list and copies or statements if, on examination, he finds them to be correct.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: .2in; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">11</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">. <strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">The plaint shall be rejected in the following cases:- </strong></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l4 level2 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(a)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where it does not disclose a cause of action; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l4 level2 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(b)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">where the relief claimed is undervalued, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to correct the valuation within a time to be fixed by the Court fails to do so; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; mso-list: l4 level2 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(c)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">    </span></span></span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">where the relief claimed is properly valued, but the plaint is written upon paper insufficiently stamped, and the plaintiff, on being required by the Court to supply the requisite stamp-paper within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails to do so; </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -.25in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l4 level2 lfo2; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .75in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">(d)<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">   </span></span></span></em></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Where the suit appears from the statement in the plaint to be barred by any law. <sup>1</sup>[:]</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><sup><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">1</span></sup></em><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">[Provided that the time fixed by the Court for the correction of the valuation or supplying of the requisite stamp-paper shall not exceed twenty-one days].</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .5in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><sup><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">2</span></sup></em><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">[(e) Where any of the provisions of rule 9 (1A) is not complied with and the plaintiff on being required by the Court to comply therewith within a time to be fixed by the Court, fails to do so.]<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">”</strong> </span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">28.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the provisions of Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code it is clearly divulged that the provision can only invoke on an application only to reject the plaint. The application filed in the Miscellaneous Case which is not a plaint, now the question is in the instant Miscellaneous Case the pre-emptee as applicant can invoke the Rule 11 of Order 7 of the Code of Civil Procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">29.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">To determine the question whether Miscellaneous case under section 96 of the Act can be rejected through such an application under Rule 11 of Order VII of the Code. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">30.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">To draw the differences between the plaint and the application of pre-emption case we must refer to the provisions Rule 1 to 9 of order VII of the Code because the legislator codified the requirements of the plaint for different class of suit as quoted in Rules 1-9 in the Order 7 of the Code but we do not find any such provision of law for the application under section 96 of the Act. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">31.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Besides the above legal proposition another prescribed form has been laid down in Sub-Rule 44 of Rule 774 of the Civil Rule’s and Order for filing application of pre-emption case. In the referred sub rule it has been shown that any application under section 96 of the <span style="letter-spacing: -.3pt;">Act, 1950 would be registered as Miscellaneous</span> Case. Therefore, it is crystal clear that such an application cannot be treated as suit and description given in the application cannot be treated as pleading of plaint.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">32.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Moreover, in pre-emption case never drawn up a decree after its disposal but, if the suit is dispose of in either way decree must be drawn up to that effect. So, it is crystal clear that the final order passed in a pre-emption case it is an order not decree.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">33.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Now to determine the difference between the decree and order we must looked into the provision of section 2 of the Code wherein the definition of order and decree has been given. We are of the view that it would be profitable to reproduce the definition of the decree and order which runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .2in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">    </span>(2) “<strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;">decree</strong>” means the formal expression of an adjudication which, so far as regards the Court expressing it, conclusively determines the rights of the parties with regard to all or any of the matters in controversy in the suit and may be either preliminary or final.<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>It shall be deemed to include the rejection of a plaint and the determination of any question within <sup>3</sup>* * * *</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt .2in;"><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">(14) “order”means the formal expression of any decision of a Civil Court which is not a decree:</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">34.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">From the above definition we can conclude the difference between the decree and order, since in the pre-emption case no decree would be drawn up after disposal but if the application for Miscellaneous Case is rejected under order 7 Rule 11 in that situation decree must be drawn up because in the definition of the decree it has been clearly opined that Court itself be deemed to include the rejection of a plaint as decree. It is, therefore, crystal clear that the application under order 7 Rule 11 of the Code cannot invoke in the case in hand, because an application under section 96 of the Act is dispose of finally by an order, obviously not by a decree. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">35.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">However, Mr. Purnindu Bikash Das advanced his submission referring section 141 of the Code wherein it has been enacted by the legislature that the provision of section 141 would be applicable in the proceedings of the Miscellaneous case in the Court of civil jurisdiction therefore, it would be noteworthy to reproduce the provision of section 141 herein below which runs as follows:- </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">141. </span></strong><em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">The procedure provided in this Code in regard to suits shall be followed, as far as it can be made applicable, in all proceedings in any Court of civil jurisdiction.</span></em></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">36.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">On perusal of the provision of section 141 it is our considered view that this section would be applicable only for procedural matter so far it can be made applicable. Therefore, we are of the opinion that section 141 of the Code cannot be invoked at the time of passing the substantive justice. From the above discussion in respect of order and decree which determine substantive justice or any of the party in a proceeding resolving the controversy in between the parties through decree but not by order. In a present case it appears that the learned Advocate filed an application under order 7 Rule 11 of the Code and impleading the said provision of law and resorted to reject the plaint but we find no plaint in the present case rather, it is an application which has been registered as Miscellaneous case (Pre-emption). </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">37.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">So, it is obvious that an application under 96 of the State Acquisition and Tenancy Act does not come in the category of a suit. It just an application for the purpose of pre-emption as prescribed by the special law which cannot, therefore, be equated with a suit because none of the requirements of a suit such as regular plaint, Court fees, written statement and decree etc is attracted to such an application. On the aforementioned discussions it is crystal clear that the application for Miscellaneous case cannot be rejected under order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">38.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Purnindu Bikash Das further advanced his submission referring section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure and submits that miss-quoting and non-quoting of provision of law by the learned Advocate on an application cannot be the sole basis for passing the appropriate order, if from the contentions of the application it appear that any question of law has been raised in respect of any proceedings for ends of justice and to protect abuse of process of law the Court. The Court himself can invoke the inherent jurisdiction of<span style="mso-spacerun: yes;">  </span>under section 151 of the Code for exercising the jurisdiction for ends of justice. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">39.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">He very candidly submitted that the learned lawyer of the trial Court filed application under order 7 Rule 11 instead of 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure only for this reason a illegal proceedings cannot be proceeded since it has clearly been mentioned in the application under order 7 Rule 11 that the proceeding is illegal and if such illegal proceeding going on that would be tantamount abuse of process of the Court as well as both the parties in the litigation could not get any result after the conclusion of the trial because the future result of the instant proceeding is as clear as day light therefore, such unfounded proceedings must be buried in its inception. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">40.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In view of the submission of the learned Advocate for the petitioner we find support from the principles enunciated in the case of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Abdul Jalil and others Vs. Islamic Bank Bangladesh Limited and others reported in 53 DLR (AD) (2001)12 </em>wherein the apex Court has held that – </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 2;">               </span>“<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">It is well settled that where a plaint cannot be rejected under Order 7 Rule 11 of the Code of Civil Procedure the court may invoke its inherent jurisdiction and reject the plaint taking recourse to section 151 of the Code of Civil Procedure</em>.” </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;"><span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">         </span>It has been further held that – “<em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">As the ultimate result of the suit is as clear as day light such a suit must be burried at its inception so that no further time is consumed in a fruitless litigation.”</em></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">41.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">In the case in hand regarding the legal provision as to the maintainability we have already discussed elsewhere in the judgment. Our such view is supportive to the case of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Mojibar Rahman Mondal (Md) Vs. Khoteza Khatoon and others reported in 2 BLC(AD) (1997)170 </em>wherein the apex Court himself found that the principle of excepting the rest amount of the deposit to file an application under section 96 of the Act, 1950 beyond the statutory period is not maintainable. </span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level2 lfo1; tab-stops: 27.0pt list 1.0in; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">42.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">        </span></span></span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">We have also find support of our view from the discussion regarding the partial pre-emption to the case of <em style="mso-bidi-font-style: normal;">Hatem Ali Mollah &amp; others Vs. Hayet Khan &amp; others reported in 1986 BCR(AD)237.</em></span></p><div style="mso-element: footnote-list;"><br clear="all"/><hr align="left" size="1" width="33%"/><div id="ftn1" style="mso-element: footnote;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><a href="#_ftnref1" name="_ftn1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">Civil Revision No. </span></strong></a><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt;">1584 of 2016</span></strong></p></div></div></div></div>
623	<h2 class="blog_entry-title">Bangladesh Vs. Md. Ataur Rahman and others </h2>
<div class="entry-content"><div class="entry-content"><p><b>Case No:</b> CIVIL APPEAL No. 41 of 2011 </p><p><b>Judge:</b>  Md. Muzammel Hossain,C,J</p><p><b>Court:</b> Appellate Division ,</p><p><b>Advocate:</b> Mr. Abdur Rob Chowdhury, Senior Advocate, Mr. Rokonuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate, Mr. Murad Reza, Additional Attoreny General, ,</p><p><b>Citation:</b>  2018(1) LNJ (AD)  </p><p><b>Case Year:</b>  2015</p><p><b>Appellant:</b>  Bangladesh, represented by the Cabinet Secretary, Cabinet Division, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka, 1000. </p><p><b>Respondent:</b>  Md. Ataur Rahman and others </p><p><b>Subject:</b>  Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972 &amp; Warrant of Precedence, 1986</p><p><b>Delivery Date:</b>  2018-06-05</p><!DOCTYPE html><p><!-- [if Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="63" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Shading 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 1 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="68" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 2 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="69" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Medium Grid 3 Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="70" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Dark List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="71" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Shading Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="72" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful List Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="73" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Colorful Grid Accent 5"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="60" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Shading Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="61" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light List Accent 6"/>  <w:LsdException Locked="false" Priority="62" SemiHidden="false"   UnhideWhenUsed="false" Name="Light Grid Accent 6"/> text-align: center; line-height: 200%;"><a href="#_ftn1" name="_ftnref1" style="mso-footnote-id: ftn1;" title=""><span class="MsoFootnoteReference"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 200%; font-family: Symbol; mso-ascii-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-hansi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-char-type: symbol; mso-symbol-font-family: Symbol;"><span style="mso-char-type: symbol; padding: 0in 5.4pt; height: 112.85pt;"><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Bangladesh, represented by the Cabinet Secretary, Cabinet Division, Bangladesh Secretariat, Dhaka, 1000. </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 6.0pt; text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . .<u>Appellant</u></span></em></strong></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">-Versus-</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">Md. Ataur Rahman and others </span></p><p align="right" class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: right;"><strong><em><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman';">. . . <u>Respondents</u></span></em></strong></p></td></tr></tbody></table><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-top: .25in; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Warrant of Precedence being arbitrary, irrational, whimsical and capricious is subject to judicial review—The High Court Division having considered the respective status and positions of different constitutional functionaries and the persons in service of the Republic rightly held that though impugned Warrant of Precedence is a policy decision of the Government yet “in the absence of evidence of any discernible guidelines, objective standards, criteria or yardsticks upon-which the impugned Warrant of Precedence ought to be predicated, we feel constrained to hold that the said Warrant of Precedence cannot shrug off the disqualification of being arbitrary, irrational, whimsical and capricious and is, therefore, subject to judicial review under Article 102 of the Constitution.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">        </span>. . .(50)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Articles 102 and 116A</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 105%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Members of the judicial service are not holders of the constitutional posts but they being public servants are in the service of the Republic, ends of justice would be best served if the District Judges and equivalent judicial officers are placed in the same table of the Warrant of Precedence along with the Secretaries and equivalent public servants. There is no denying that members of the judicial service (i.e., the subordinate judiciary) are not holders of the constitutional posts but they being public servants are in the service of the Republic and the nature of their service is totally different from the civil administrative executives. District Judges and holders of the equivalent judicial posts are the highest posts in the subordinate judiciary. In view of the provisions of the Article 116A of the Constitution all persons employed in the judicial service and all magistrates exercising judicial functions shall be independent in the exercise of their judicial functions, so it is immaterial to say that members of judicial service or the subordinate judiciary are above the senior administrative and defence executives.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">                                        </span>. . . (62)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Constitution of Bangladesh, 1972</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Article 102</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The High Court Division as well as the Appellate Division is competent enough to give necessary directions to follow the mandate of the Constitution: When there is a deviation from the constitutional arrangements or constitutional arrangements have been interfered with or altered by the Government or when the Government fails to implement the provisions of Chapter II of Part VI of the Constitution and instead follow a different course not sanctioned by the Constitution, the High Court Division as well as the Appellate Division is competent enough to give necessary directions to follow the mandate of the Constitution. This means the Apex Court of the Country is competent to issue directions upon the authorities concerned to perform their obligatory duties whenever there is a failure on their part to discharge their duties.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">     </span>. . . (68</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Warrant of Precedence, 1986</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Civil awards holders and holders of gallantry awards of Bir Uttam should be included in the Warrant of Precedence the Warrant of Precedence of the neighbouring countries include the holders of highest civil awards, however the impugned Warrant of Precedence of our country does not include such dignitaries, who are not constitutional or </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">public functionaries. As such, it is expected</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> that those dignitaries who have been honoured or decorated with civil </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">awards, e.i., Shadhinata Padak, or Ekhushey</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> Padak, and those valiant freedom fighters who have been honoured with gallantry awards of Bir Uttam should be included in the Table of the impugned Warrant of Precedence in such order as deemed appropriate.<span style="mso-tab-count: 1;">           </span>. . . (69)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Warrant of Precedence, 1986</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The impugned Warrant of Precedence being based on utter irrationality and arbitrariness is to be modified and amended in the following manner:</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">1) As the Constitution is the supreme law </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.3pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">of the land, all constitutional functionaries</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> shall be placed first in order of priority in the Table of the impugned Warrant of Precedence. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">2) Members of judicial service holding the posts of District Judges or equivalent posts of District Judges shall be placed at Serial No.16 in the Table along with the Secretaries to the Government and equivalent public servants in the service of the Republic. </span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: right 210.85pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">3) Additional District Judges or holders of equivalent judicial posts shall be </span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; letter-spacing: -.4pt; mso-ansi-language: EN;">placed at the serial number 17 immediately</span></strong><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"> after the District Judges. . . . (70)</span></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -31.7pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 2.95in 224.2pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Appellant:</span></strong> <span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">Mr. Abdur Rob Chowdhury, Senior Advocate, instructed by Mrs. Sufia Khatun, Advocate-On-Record.<u> </u></span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -31.7pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 2.95in 224.2pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Respondent No. 1</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">: Mr. Rokonuddin Mahmud, Senior Advocate with Mr. Asaduzzaman, Advocte, instructed by Mr. Syed Mahbubar Rahman, Advocate-On-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -31.7pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 2.95in 224.2pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Respondent No. 2</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">: Mr. Murad Reza, Additional Attoreny General, instructed by Mrs. Mahmuda Begum, Advocate-On-Record.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: -31.7pt; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 2.95in 224.2pt; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 1.0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">For the Respondent No. 3</span></strong><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">: Mr. Murad Reza, Additional Attoreny General, instructed by Mr. Nawab Ali, Advocate-On-Record.</span></p><p align="center" class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: center; line-height: 110%;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><u><span style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%;">JUDGMENT</span></u></strong></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="margin-bottom: 12.0pt; text-align: justify; text-indent: 27.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none;"><strong><u><span lang="EN" style="font-family: 'Times New Roman Bold','serif'; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; font-variant: small-caps; mso-ansi-language: EN;">Md. Muzammel Hossain, CJ:</span></u></strong> <span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">This appeal, by leave, is directed against the impugned judgment and order dated 04.02.2010 passed by a Division Bench of the High Court Division in Writ Petition No.11685 of 2006 making the Rule absolute in modified form declaring the impugned Warrant of Precedence 1986 without lawful authority and of no legal effect and directing the writ Respondent No.1 to prepare a new Warrant of Precedence on the basis of the eight-point directives within 60(sixty) days of receipt of the judgment placing the District Judges, Additional District Judges, Chief Judicial Magistrates and Chief Metropolitan Magistrates in the same table above the Chiefs of Staff of the Defence Service of Bangladesh in the Warrant of Precedence.</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 6.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">2.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">The facts for disposal of this appeal, in brief, are that the writ petitioner-respondent No.1 while serving as an Additional District and Sessions Judge and holding the Office of Secretary-General of Bangladesh Judicial Service Association filed writ petition No.11685 of 2006 under Article 102 of the Constitution challenging Warrant of Precedence, 1986 (revised up to 12.04.2000), issued vide Cabinet Division’s Notification No.CD-10/1/85-Rules/161, dated 11.09.1986 by the Writ respondent No.1, the appellant placing the members of judicial service and Constitutional posts equally with or subordinating them to the employees of the Republic particularly to the administrative cadres, in contravention to the spirit of the Constitution. A Division Bench of the High Court Division heard the petition and being satisfied issued Rule Nisi on the following terms:</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; line-height: 110%; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 27.0pt;"><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">“Let a Rule Nisi be issued calling upon the respondents to show cause as to why the impugned Warrant of Precedence issued vide Cabinet Division’s Notification No.CD- 10/1/85- Rules/161, dated 11.09.1986 as revised up to 12.04.2000 (Annexure-A to the writ petition) equating with or subordinating District Judges and other judicial officers equivalent to the rank of District Judges to the concerned officers of the administrative and other cadres therein should not be declared to have been issued without lawful authority and to be of no legal effect and why the respondents should not be directed to place District Judges and other judicial officers holding the rank of District Judges are on a par with the holders of Constitutional posts and above he positions of the persons in the service of the Republic in the aforesaid Warrant of Precedence and/or such other or further order or orders passed as to this Court may seem fit and proper.”</span></p><p class="MsoNormal" style="text-align: justify; text-indent: 0in; line-height: 110%; mso-list: l2 level1 lfo2; tab-stops: 27.0pt; mso-layout-grid-align: none; text-autospace: none; margin: 0in 0in 12.0pt 0in;"><strong style="mso-bidi-font-weight: normal;"><span lang="EN" style="font-size: 11.0pt; line-height: 110%; mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;"><span style="mso-list: Ignore;">3.<span style="font: 7.0pt 'Times New Roman';">            </span></span></span></strong><span lang="EN" style="mso-bidi-font-family: 'Times New Roman'; mso-ansi-language: EN;">It has been stated that the writ petitioner filed the writ petition in his capacity as a concerned, affected and aggrieved person to protect the interest of indefinite number of people of Bangladesh and to uphold the Rule of Law by way of public interest litigation and to prevent illegal and arbitrary placement of the members of the judicial service and the Constitutional Office holders in inappropriate places in the Warrant of Precedence in derogation of their dignity and status in public perception.
